The Call of the Siren

In Greek mythology, sirens are human-like beings with alluring voices; they appear in a scene in the Odyssey in which Odysseus saves his crew's lives. Roman poets place them on some small islands called ‘‘Sirenum scopuli’’. In some later, rationalized traditions, the literal geography of the ‘‘flowery’’ island of Anthemoessa, or Anthemusa, is fixed: sometimes on Cape Pelorum and at others in the islands known as the Sirenuse, near Paestum, or in Capreae. All such locations were surrounded by cliffs and rocks.

This is why no one could have foreseen one appearing in America.

The first recorded individual of the species, a supposed white male from Vermont calling itself ‘‘Howard Brush Dean III’’, first became of public interest in 1991, when it became Governor of the state following the death of his predecessor, Richard A. Snelling, by a supposed heart attack. Serving in the office until 2003, the creature later mounted a campaign to become the next President of the United States. This is when it first demonstrated its full power.

On January 19th, 2004, following his victory in the Iowa Caucus, the entity unleashed a sonic rallying cry to his supporters, instantly entrancing them. The cry would be covered on news station after news station; exactly as planned. Soon, the entire country, and a significant portion of the world, was under its control.

Instead of leading them to their deaths, however, ‘‘Dean’’ would use his powers to win. And win. And win again. The 22nd Amendment was repealed unanimously, to let the entity continue running for President. The Senate and House were both abolished. The entire government of the United States was soon disbanded, in favor of reforming the nation into the First American Empire, with Dean as its Emperor.

And yet, that was only the beginning.
